<ul class="mw-collapsible-content" style="margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit; list-style: none; margin-left: 0;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1316064257" /><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Windows</th><td class="infobox-data">January 2026 Update (19.2601.57101.0) / 2&#160;February 2026<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;24 days ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2026-02-02</span>)</span><sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Android</th><td class="infobox-data">16.0 (Build 19530.20024) / 10&#160;December 2025<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;2 months ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2025-12-10</span>)</span><sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">iOS<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ios&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ios-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></th><td class="infobox-data">2.106.2 / 29&#160;January 2026<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;28 days ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2026-01-29</span>)</span><sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
</li></ul>
</div>
   </div></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;">Written in</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a> (back-end),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-C++&#95;in&#95;MS&#95;Office&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C++_in_MS_Office-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Objective-C" title="Objective-C">Objective-C</a> (API/UI on Mac)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-C++&#95;in&#95;MS&#95;Office&#95;9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C++_in_MS_Office-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">Operating system</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sysreq-365&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sysreq-365-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> (current versions)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Computing_platform" title="Computing platform">Platform</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/IA-32" title="IA-32">IA-32</a>, <a href="/wiki/X86-64" title="X86-64">x86-64</a>, <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture_family" title="ARM architecture family">Arm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arm64" class="mw-redirect" title="Arm64">Arm64</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;">Predecessor</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Multi-Tool_Word" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-Tool Word">Multi-Tool Word</a> or <a href="/wiki/WordPad" title="WordPad">WordPad</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Software_categories#Categorization_approaches" title="Software categories">Type</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Word_processor" title="Word processor">Word processor</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Software_license" title="Software license">License</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Trialware" class="mw-redirect" title="Trialware">Trialware</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/word">microsoft<wbr />.com<wbr />/en-us<wbr />/microsoft-365<wbr />/word</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table> <p><b>Microsoft Word</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Word_processor_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Word processor program">word processing program</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>. It was first released on October 25, 1983,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> under the original name <b>Multi-Tool Word</b> for <a href="/wiki/Xenix" title="Xenix">Xenix</a> systems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-PCHistory&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCHistory-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Subsequent versions were later written for several other platforms including <a href="/wiki/IBM_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="IBM PC">IBM PCs</a> running <a href="/wiki/DOS" title="DOS">DOS</a> (1983), <a href="/wiki/Apple_Macintosh" class="mw-redirect" title="Apple Macintosh">Apple Macintosh</a> running the <a href="/wiki/Classic_Mac_OS" title="Classic Mac OS">Classic Mac OS</a> (1985), <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_UNIX_PC" title="AT&amp;T UNIX PC">AT&amp;T UNIX PC</a> (1985), <a href="/wiki/Atari_ST" title="Atari ST">Atari ST</a> (1988), <a href="/wiki/OS/2" title="OS/2">OS/2</a> (1989), <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> (1989), <a href="/wiki/SCO_Unix" class="mw-redirect" title="SCO Unix">SCO Unix</a> (1990), <a href="/wiki/Handheld_PC" title="Handheld PC">Handheld PC</a> (1996), <a href="/wiki/Pocket_PC" title="Pocket PC">Pocket PC</a> (2000), <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a> (2001), <a href="/wiki/Web_browsers" class="mw-redirect" title="Web browsers">Web browsers</a> (2010), <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> (2014), and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> (2015).
</p><p>Microsoft Word has been the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> standard word processing software since the 1990s when it eclipsed <a href="/wiki/WordPerfect" title="WordPerfect">WordPerfect</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Commercial versions of Word are licensed as a standalone product or as a component of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office" title="Microsoft Office">Microsoft Office</a>, which can be purchased with a perpetual license, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_365" title="Microsoft 365">Microsoft 365</a> suite as a <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">subscription</a>, or as a one-time purchase with <a href="/wiki/Office_2024" class="mw-redirect" title="Office 2024">Office 2024</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Microsoft_Word" title="History of Microsoft Word">History of Microsoft Word</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Word_1.0.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Word_1.0.png/250px-Word_1.0.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="157" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c1/Word_1.0.png 1.5x" data-file-width="399" data-file-height="250" /></a><figcaption>Microsoft Word 1.0 for DOS (1983) (using a black background, using font "IBM BIOS-2y")</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1981, Microsoft hired <a href="/wiki/Charles_Simonyi" title="Charles Simonyi">Charles Simonyi</a>, the primary developer of <a href="/wiki/Bravo_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bravo (software)">Bravo</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/GUI" class="mw-redirect" title="GUI">GUI</a> <a href="/wiki/Word_processor" title="Word processor">word processor</a>, which was developed at <a href="/wiki/PARC_(company)" title="PARC (company)">Xerox PARC</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcworld&#95;word25&#95;17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcworld_word25-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Simonyi started work on a word processor called <i>Multi-Tool Word</i> and soon hired <a href="/wiki/Richard_Brodie_(programmer)" title="Richard Brodie (programmer)">Richard Brodie</a>, a former Xerox intern, who became the primary software engineer.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcworld&#95;word25&#95;17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcworld_word25-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft announced Multi-Tool Word for <a href="/wiki/Xenix" title="Xenix">Xenix</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcworld&#95;word25&#95;17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcworld_word25-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and MS-DOS in 1983.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-infoworld&#95;multi-tool&#95;word&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infoworld_multi-tool_word-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its name was soon simplified to <i>Microsoft Word</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-PCHistory&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCHistory-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Free demonstration copies of the application were bundled with the November 1983 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/PC_World" title="PC World">PC World</a></i>, making it the first to be distributed on-disk with a <a href="/wiki/Magazine" title="Magazine">magazine</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-PCHistory&#95;12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCHistory-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-NYTimes19930825&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes19930825-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> That year Microsoft demonstrated Word running on <a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lemmons198312&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lemmons198312-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Unlike most <a href="/wiki/MS-DOS" title="MS-DOS">MS-DOS</a> programs at the time, Microsoft Word was designed to be used with a mouse.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-infoworld&#95;multi-tool&#95;word&#95;20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infoworld_multi-tool_word-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Advertisements depicted the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Mouse" title="Microsoft Mouse">Microsoft Mouse</a> and described Word as a <a href="/wiki/WYSIWYG" title="WYSIWYG">WYSIWYG</a> (What You See Is What You Get), windowed word processor with the ability to <a href="/wiki/Undo" title="Undo">undo</a> and display bold, italic, and underlined text,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-byte198312&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byte198312-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although it could not render <a href="/wiki/Font" title="Font">fonts</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-PCHistory&#95;12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCHistory-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was not initially popular, since its user interface was different from the leading word processor at the time, <a href="/wiki/WordStar" title="WordStar">WordStar</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, Microsoft steadily improved the product, releasing versions 2.0 through 5.0 over the next six years. In 1985, Microsoft <a href="/wiki/Porting" title="Porting">ported</a> Word to the <a href="/wiki/Classic_Mac_OS" title="Classic Mac OS">classic Mac OS</a> (known as Macintosh System Software at the time). This was made easier by Word for DOS having been designed for use with high-resolution displays and laser printers, even though none were yet available to the general public.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lowendmac&#95;history&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lowendmac_history-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was also notable for its very fast cut-and-paste function and unlimited number of undo operations, which are due to its usage of the <a href="/wiki/Piece_table" title="Piece table">piece table</a> data structure.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Following the precedents of LisaWrite and MacWrite, Word for Mac OS added true WYSIWYG features. It fulfilled a need for a word processor that was more capable than <a href="/wiki/MacWrite" title="MacWrite">MacWrite</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By 1988 <a href="/wiki/WordPerfect" title="WordPerfect">WordPerfect</a> and Word dominated the DOS word processor market, but neither product nor any other had true WYSIWYG, unlike Mac software;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-seymour19880229&#95;28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seymour19880229-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> after its release, Word for Mac OS's sales were higher than its MS-DOS counterpart for at least four years.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcworld&#95;word25&#95;17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcworld_word25-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The second release of Word for Mac OS, shipped in 1987, was named Word 3.0 to synchronize its version number with Word for DOS; this was Microsoft's first attempt to synchronize version numbers across platforms. Word 3.0 included numerous internal enhancements and new features, including the first implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Rich_Text_Format" title="Rich Text Format">Rich Text Format</a> (RTF) specification, but was plagued with bugs. Within a few months, Word 3.0 was superseded by a more stable Word 3.01, which was mailed free to all registered users of 3.0.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lowendmac&#95;history&#95;25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lowendmac_history-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After MacWrite Pro was discontinued in the mid-1990s, Word for Mac OS never had any serious rivals. Word 5.1 for Mac OS, released in 1992, was a very popular word processor owing to its elegance, relative ease of use, and feature set. Many users say it is the best version of Word for Mac OS ever created.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lowendmac&#95;history&#95;25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lowendmac_history-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-msdn&#95;macword6&#95;29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msdn_macword6-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1986, an agreement between <a href="/wiki/Atari" title="Atari">Atari</a> and Microsoft brought Word to the <a href="/wiki/Atari_ST" title="Atari ST">Atari ST</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Microsoft&#95;Write&#95;for&#95;Atari&#95;ST&#95;30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Microsoft_Write_for_Atari_ST-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> under the name <i><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Write" title="Microsoft Write">Microsoft Write</a></i>. The Atari ST version was a port of Word 1.05 for the Mac OS<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Microsoft&#95;Write&#95;for&#95;Atari&#95;ST&#95;review&#95;31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Microsoft_Write_for_Atari_ST_review-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Microsoft&#95;Word&#95;for&#95;Atari&#95;ST&#95;32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Microsoft_Word_for_Atari_ST-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and was never updated.
</p><p>By the early 1990s, the growing popularity of Windows narrowed the word processor market to a few supporting the operating system, including Word, WordPerfect, and <a href="/wiki/Ami_Pro" class="mw-redirect" title="Ami Pro">Ami Pro</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Seattle&#95;Times&#95;Nov&#95;1993&#95;33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seattle_Times_Nov_1993-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first version of Word for Windows was released in 1989. With the release of <a href="/wiki/Windows_3.0" title="Windows 3.0">Windows 3.0</a> the following year, sales began to pick up and Microsoft soon became the market leader for word processors for <a href="/wiki/IBM_Personal_Computer" title="IBM Personal Computer">IBM PC-compatible computers</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcworld&#95;word25&#95;17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcworld_word25-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1991, Microsoft capitalized on Word for Windows' increasing popularity by releasing a version of Word for DOS, version 5.5, that replaced its unique user interface with an interface similar to a Windows application.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By then Word had more than half of the Windows word processor market.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cw19920720&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cw19920720-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When Microsoft became aware of the <a href="/wiki/Year_2000_problem" title="Year 2000 problem">Year 2000 problem</a>, it made Microsoft Word 5.5 for DOS available for free downloads. As of January&#160;2026<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, it is still available for download from Microsoft's website.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
In 1991, Microsoft embarked on a project code-named Pyramid to completely rewrite Microsoft Word from the ground up. Both the Windows and Mac OS versions would start from the same code base. It was abandoned when it was determined that it would take the development team too long to rewrite and then catch up with all the new capabilities that could have been added at the same time without a rewrite. Instead, the next versions of Word for Windows and Mac OS, dubbed version 6.0, both started from the code base of Word for Windows 2.0.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-msdn&#95;macword6&#95;29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msdn_macword6-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>With the release of Word 6.0 in 1993, Microsoft again attempted to synchronize the version numbers and coordinate product naming across platforms, this time across DOS, Mac OS, and Windows (this was the last version of Word for DOS). It introduced AutoCorrect, which automatically fixed certain typing errors, and AutoFormat, which could reformat many parts of a document at once. While the Windows version received favorable reviews (e.g., from <i>InfoWorld</i><sup id="cite&#95;ref-infoworld&#95;word6&#95;38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infoworld_word6-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>), the Mac OS version was widely derided. Many accused it of being slow, clumsy, and memory intensive, and its user interface differed significantly from Word 5.1.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-msdn&#95;macword6&#95;29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msdn_macword6-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In response to user requests, Microsoft offered Word 5 again, after it had been discontinued.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ugeek&#95;97&#95;39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ugeek_97-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Subsequent versions of Word for macOS are no longer direct ports of Word for Windows, instead featuring a mixture of ported code and native code.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="File_formats">File formats</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: File formats"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1316064257" /><table class="infobox" style="width:314px"><caption class="infobox-title">Native file formats</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-image"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:.doc_icon_(2000-03).svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/.doc_icon_%282000-03%29.svg/120px-.doc_icon_%282000-03%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="66" height="65" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/.doc_icon_%282000-03%29.svg/250px-.doc_icon_%282000-03%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="94" data-file-height="92" /></a></span> <span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:.docx_icon.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/.docx_icon.svg/120px-.docx_icon.svg.png" decoding="async" width="75" height="75" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/.docx_icon.svg/250px-.docx_icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></a></span><div class="infobox-caption">Left: The icon for <code>.doc</code> files.<br />Right: The icon for <code>.docx</code> files. The file formats are differentiated by using the Word logo as seen in Office 2000 and the logo for the current version of Word.</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Doc_(computing)" title="Doc (computing)">DOC</a></th><td class="infobox-data">Legacy Word document</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">DOT</th><td class="infobox-data">Legacy Word templates</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">WBK</th><td class="infobox-data">Legacy Word document backup</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">DOCX</th><td class="infobox-data">XML Word document</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">DOCM</th><td class="infobox-data">XML Word macro-enabled document</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">DOTX</th><td class="infobox-data">XML Word template</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">DOTM</th><td class="infobox-data">XML Word macro-enabled template</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">DOCB</th><td class="infobox-data">XML Word binary document</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Filename_extensions">Filename extensions</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Filename extensions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Microsoft Word's native file formats are denoted either by a <code>.doc</code> or <code>.docx</code> <a href="/wiki/Filename_extension" title="Filename extension">filename extension</a>.
</p><p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Doc_(computing)" title="Doc (computing)"><code>.<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1239334494">'"`UNIQ--templatestyles-0000004A-QINU`"'</style><span class="tmp-color" style="color:blue">doc</span></code></a> extension has been used in many different versions of Word, it actually encompasses four distinct file formats:
</p>
<ol><li>Word for DOS</li>
<li>Word for Windows 1 and 2; Word 3 and 4 for Mac OS</li>
<li>Word 6 and Word 95 for Windows; Word 6 for Mac OS</li>
<li>Word 97 and later for Windows; Word 98 and later for Mac OS</li></ol>
<p>(The <a href="/wiki/Classic_Mac_OS" title="Classic Mac OS">classic Mac OS</a> of the era did not use filename extensions.)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The newer <code>.docx</code> extension signifies the <a href="/wiki/Standardization_of_Office_Open_XML" title="Standardization of Office Open XML">Office Open XML international standard</a> for Office documents and is used by default by Word 2007 and later for Windows as well as Word 2008 and later for macOS.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Binary_formats_(Word_97–2007)"><span id="Binary_formats_.28Word_97.E2.80.932007.29"></span>Binary formats (Word 97–2007)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Binary formats (Word 97–2007)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>During the late 1990s and early 2000s, the default Word document format (<a href="/wiki/DOC_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="DOC (computing)">.DOC</a>) became a <i>de facto</i> standard of <a href="/wiki/Document_file_format" title="Document file format">document file formats</a> for Microsoft Office users.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> There are different versions of "Word Document Format" used by default in Word 97–2007.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Each binary word file is a <a href="/wiki/Compound_File_Binary_Format" title="Compound File Binary Format">Compound File</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a hierarchical <a href="/wiki/File_system" title="File system">file system</a> within a file. According to <a href="/wiki/Joel_Spolsky" title="Joel Spolsky">Joel Spolsky</a>, Word Binary File Format is extremely complex mainly because its developers had to accommodate an overwhelming number of features and prioritize performance over anything else.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-spolsky-commentry&#95;44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spolsky-commentry-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As with all OLE Compound Files, Word Binary Format consists of "storages", which are analogous to <a href="/wiki/Folder_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Folder (computing)">computer folders</a>, and "streams", which are similar to <a href="/wiki/Computer_file" title="Computer file">computer files</a>. Each storage may contain streams or other storage. Each Word Binary File must contain a stream called the "WordDocument" stream and this stream must start with a File Information Block (FIB).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> FIB serves as the first point of reference for locating everything else, such as where the text in a Word document starts, ends, what version of Word created the document and other attributes.
</p><p>Word 2007 and later continue to support the DOC file format, although it is no longer the default.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="XML_Document_(Word_2003)"><span id="XML_Document_.28Word_2003.29"></span>XML Document (Word 2003)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: XML Document (Word 2003)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office_XML_formats" title="Microsoft Office XML formats">Microsoft Office XML formats</a></div>
<p>The .docx XML format introduced in Word 2003<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> was a simple, <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>-based format called <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office_XML_formats#File_formats" title="Microsoft Office XML formats">WordProcessingML or WordML.</a>
</p><p>The <b>Microsoft Office XML formats</b> are <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>-based document formats (or <a href="/wiki/XML_schema" title="XML schema">XML schemas</a>) introduced in versions of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office" title="Microsoft Office">Microsoft Office</a> prior to <a href="/wiki/Office_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Office 2007">Office 2007</a>. <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office_XP" title="Microsoft Office XP">Microsoft Office XP</a> introduced a new XML format for storing Excel spreadsheets and Office 2003 added an XML-based format for Word documents.
</p><p>These formats were succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Office_Open_XML" title="Office Open XML">Office Open XML</a> (ECMA-376) in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office_2007" title="Microsoft Office 2007">Microsoft Office 2007</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cross-version_compatibility">Cross-version compatibility</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Cross-version compatibility"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Opening a Word Document file in a version of Word other than the one with which it was created can cause an incorrect display of the document. The document formats of the various versions change in subtle and not-so-subtle ways (such as changing the font or the handling of more complex tasks like footnotes). Formatting created in newer versions does not always survive when viewed in older versions of the program, nearly always because that capability does not exist in the previous version.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-casson&#95;ryan&#95;47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-casson_ryan-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rich_Text_Format" title="Rich Text Format">Rich Text Format</a> (RTF), an early effort to create a format for interchanging formatted text between applications, is an optional format for Word that retains most formatting and all content of the original document.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Third-party_formats">Third-party formats</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Third-party formats"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Plugin_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plugin (computing)">Plugins</a> permitting the Windows versions of Word to read and write formats it does not natively support, such as <a href="/wiki/International_standard" title="International standard">international standard</a> <a href="/wiki/OpenDocument" title="OpenDocument">OpenDocument</a> format (ODF) (ISO/IEC 26300:2006), are available. Up until the release of <a href="/wiki/Windows_XP#Service_packs" title="Windows XP">Service Pack 2</a> (SP2) for Office 2007, Word did not natively support reading or writing ODF documents without a plugin, namely the SUN ODF Plugin or the OpenXML/ODF Translator. With SP2 installed, ODF format 1.1 documents can be read and saved like any other supported format in addition to those already available in Word 2007.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-casson&#95;ryan&#95;47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-casson_ryan-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The implementation faces <a href="/wiki/OpenDocument_software#Microsoft_Office_2007_SP2_support_controversy" class="mw-redirect" title="OpenDocument software">substantial criticism</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/ODF_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="ODF Alliance">ODF Alliance</a> and others have claimed that the third-party plugins provide better support.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sp2-fact-sheet&#95;52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sp2-fact-sheet-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft later declared that the ODF support has some limitations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2005, one year before the Microsoft Office 2007 suite was released, Microsoft declared that there was insufficient demand from Microsoft customers for the international standard OpenDocument format support and that therefore it would not be included in Microsoft Office 2007. This statement was repeated in the following months.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-office12-pdf&#95;54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-office12-pdf-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-odf-must&#95;55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odf-must-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-gates-odf&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gates-odf-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-odf&#95;57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odf-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As an answer, on October 20, 2005, an online petition was created to demand ODF support from Microsoft.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-petition&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-petition-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2006, the ODF plugin for Microsoft Office was released by the OpenDocument Foundation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-mso-odf-plugin&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mso-odf-plugin-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft declared that it had no relationship with the developers of the plugin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-odf&#95;57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odf-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2006, Microsoft announced the creation of the Open XML Translator project – tools to build a technical bridge between the Microsoft Office Open XML Formats and the OpenDocument Format (ODF). This work was started in response to government requests for interoperability with ODF. The goal of the project was not to add ODF support to Microsoft Office, but only to create a plugin and an external toolset.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ms-odf-plugin&#95;60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ms-odf-plugin-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In February 2007, this project released a first version of the ODF plugin for Microsoft Word.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2007, Sun released an initial version of its ODF plugin for Microsoft Office.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Version 1.0 was released in July 2007.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft Word 2007 (Service Pack 1) supports (for output only) <a href="/wiki/Portable_Document_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable Document Format">PDF</a> and <a href="/wiki/XML_Paper_Specification" class="mw-redirect" title="XML Paper Specification">XPS</a> formats, but only after manual installation of the Microsoft "Save as PDF or XPS" add-on.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On later releases, this was offered by default.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Features">Features</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1305433154">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output
