<p>Among its features, Word includes a built-in spell checker, a thesaurus, a dictionary, and utilities for manipulating and editing text. It supports creating <a href="/wiki/Table_(information)" title="Table (information)">tables</a>. Depending on the version, it can perform simple and complex calculations, and supports formatting <a href="/wiki/Formula" title="Formula">formulas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equation" title="Equation">equations</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The following are some aspects of its feature set.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Templates">Templates</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Templates"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Several later versions of Word include the ability for users to create their own formatting templates, allowing them to define a file in which: the title, heading, paragraph, and other element designs differ from the standard Word templates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Users can find how to do this under the Help section located near the top right corner (Word 2013 on <a href="/wiki/Windows_8" title="Windows 8">Windows 8</a>).
</p><p>For example, <b>Normal.dotm</b> is the master <a href="/wiki/Template_(word_processing)" title="Template (word processing)">template</a> from which all Word documents are created. It determines the <a href="/wiki/Margin_(typography)" title="Margin (typography)">margin</a> defaults as well as the layout of the text and font defaults. Although Normal.dotm is already set with certain defaults, the user can change it to new defaults. This will change other documents which were created using the template.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was previously Normal.dot.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Image_formats">Image formats</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Image formats"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Word can import and display images in common bitmap formats such as <a href="/wiki/JPEG" title="JPEG">JPG</a> and <a href="/wiki/GIF" title="GIF">GIF</a>. It can also be used to create and display simple line art. Microsoft Word added support<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> for the common <a href="/wiki/Scalable_vector_graphics" class="mw-redirect" title="Scalable vector graphics">SVG</a> vector image format in 2017 for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_365" title="Microsoft 365">Office 365</a> ProPlus subscribers and this functionality was also included in the Office 2019 release.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="WordArt">WordArt</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: WordArt"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/WordArt" class="mw-redirect" title="WordArt">WordArt</a></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:WordArt.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/WordArt.png/250px-WordArt.png" decoding="async" width="164" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/WordArt.png/330px-WordArt.png 2x" data-file-width="455" data-file-height="417" /></a><figcaption>An example image created with WordArt</figcaption></figure>
<p>WordArt enables drawing text in a Microsoft Word document such as a title, watermark, or other text, with graphical effects such as skewing, shadowing, rotating, stretching in a variety of shapes and colors, and even including three-dimensional effects. Users can apply formatting effects such as shadow, bevel, glow, and reflection to their document text as easily as applying bold or underline. Users can also spell-check text that uses visual effects and add text effects to paragraph styles.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Macros">Macros</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Macros"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Macro_(computer_science)" title="Macro (computer science)">Macros</a> may be used for frequent or repetitive sequences of keystrokes and mouse movements. Like other <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office" title="Microsoft Office">Microsoft Office</a> documents, Word files can include advanced macros and even embedded programs. The language was originally <a href="/wiki/WordBasic" class="mw-redirect" title="WordBasic">WordBasic</a>, but changed to <a href="/wiki/Visual_Basic_for_Applications" title="Visual Basic for Applications">Visual Basic for Applications</a> as of Word 97.
</p><p>This extensive functionality can also be used to run and propagate <a href="/wiki/Computer_virus" title="Computer virus">viruses</a> in documents. The tendency for people to exchange Word documents via email, <a href="/wiki/USB_flash_drive" title="USB flash drive">USB flash drives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Floppy_disk" title="Floppy disk">floppy disks</a> made this an especially attractive vector in 1999. A prominent example was the <a href="/wiki/Melissa_virus" class="mw-redirect" title="Melissa virus">Melissa virus</a>, but countless others have existed.
</p><p>These macro viruses were the only known cross-platform threats between Windows and Macintosh computers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft released patches for Word X and Word 2004 that effectively eliminated the macro problem on the Mac by 2006.
</p><p>Word's macro security setting, which regulates when macros may execute, can be adjusted by the user, but in the most recent versions of Word, it is set to HIGH by default, generally reducing the risk from macro-based viruses, which have become uncommon.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Layout_issues">Layout issues</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Layout issues"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Before Word 2010 (Word 14) for Windows, the program was unable to correctly handle <a href="/wiki/Ligature_(typography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ligature (typography)">ligatures</a> defined in <a href="/wiki/OpenType" title="OpenType">OpenType</a> fonts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Those ligature glyphs with <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> codepoints may be inserted manually, but are not recognized by Word for what they are, breaking spell checking, while custom ligatures present in the font are not accessible at all. Since Word 2010, the program now has advanced <a href="/wiki/Typesetting" title="Typesetting">typesetting</a> features which can be enabled,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/OpenType" title="OpenType">OpenType</a> ligatures,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kerning" title="Kerning">kerning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyphenation_algorithm" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyphenation algorithm">hyphenation</a> (previous versions already had the latter two features). Other layout deficiencies of Word include the inability to set crop marks or thin spaces. Various third-party workaround utilities have been developed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In Word 2004 for Mac OS X, support of <a href="/wiki/Complex_scripts" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex scripts">complex scripts</a> was inferior even to Word 97<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Word 2004 did not support <a href="/wiki/Apple_Advanced_Typography" title="Apple Advanced Typography">Apple Advanced Typography</a> features like ligatures or glyph variants.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Issues_with_technical_documents">Issues with technical documents</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Issues with technical documents"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Microsoft Word is only partially suitable for some kinds of technical writing, specifically, that which requires mathematical equations,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> figure placement, table placement and cross-references to any of these items.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The usual workaround for equations is to use a third-party equation typesetter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Figures and tables must be placed manually; there is an anchor mechanism but it is not designed for fully automatic figure placement, and editing text after placing figures and tables often requires re-placing those items by moving the anchor point, and even then the placement options are limited.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> This problem is deeply baked into Word's structure since 1985, as it does not know where page breaks will occur until the document is printed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bullets_and_numbering">Bullets and numbering</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Bullets and numbering"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Microsoft Word supports <a href="/wiki/Bullet_list" class="mw-redirect" title="Bullet list">bullet lists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Numbered_list" class="mw-redirect" title="Numbered list">numbered lists</a>. It also features a numbering system that helps add correct numbers to pages, chapters, headers, footnotes, and entries of tables of content; these numbers automatically change to correct ones as new items are added or existing items are deleted. Bullets and numbering can be applied directly to paragraphs and converted to lists.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Word 97 through 2003, however, had problems adding correct numbers to numbered lists. In particular, a second irrelevant numbered list might have not started with number one but instead resumed numbering after the last numbered list. Although Word 97 supported a hidden marker that said the list numbering must restart afterward, the command to insert this marker (Restart Numbering command) was only added in Word 2003. However, if one were to <a href="/wiki/Cut,_copy,_and_paste" title="Cut, copy, and paste">cut the first item of the listed and paste it</a> as another item (e.g. fifth), then the restart marker would have moved with it and the list would have restarted in the middle instead of at the top.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word continues to default to non-Unicode characters and non-hierarchical bulleting, despite user preference for PowerPoint-style symbol hierarchies (e.g., filled circle/emdash/filled square/endash/emptied circle) and universal compatibility.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="AutoSummarize">AutoSummarize</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: AutoSummarize"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Available in certain versions of Word (e.g., Word 2007), AutoSummarize highlights passages or phrases that it considers valuable and can be a quick way of generating a crude abstract or an executive summary.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The amount of text to be retained can be specified by the user as a percentage of the current amount of text.
</p><p>According to Ron Fein of the Word 97 team, AutoSummarize cuts wordy copy to the bone by counting words and ranking sentences. First, AutoSummarize identifies the most common words in the document (barring "a" and "the" and the like) and assigns a "score" to each word – the more frequently a word is used, the higher the score. Then, it "averages" each sentence by adding the scores of its words and dividing the sum by the number of words in the sentence – the higher the average, the higher the rank of the sentence. "It's like the ratio of wheat to chaff," explains Fein.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>AutoSummarize was removed from Microsoft Word for Mac OS X 2011, although it was present in Word for Mac 2008. AutoSummarize was removed from the Office 2010 release version (14) as well.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Spike">Spike</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Spike"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b>Spike</b> is a specialized <a href="/wiki/Cut-and-paste" class="mw-redirect" title="Cut-and-paste">cut</a> command in Microsoft Word. It is named after <a href="/wiki/Spindle_(stationery)" title="Spindle (stationery)">an implement in restaurants on which receipts are impaled</a>, and similarly sequentially stores data to be pasted and adds them together to the document when the second function step, or paste, is performed. Spiking (CONTROL–F3) performs a cut function, which can be immediately undone to simulate a "copy" command, while the pasting function (SHIFT–CONTROL–F3) will also clear the data from the spike, although this can be avoided by using alternatives to the three-key shortcut.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hidden_text">Hidden text</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hidden text"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Word supports marking selected text as "<a href="/wiki/Hidden_text" title="Hidden text">hidden</a>". Hidden text is text that is stored in the document but is not displayed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, pages containing large amounts of <a href="/wiki/Markup_language" title="Markup language">markup language</a> text can be made visually more readable during the editing process.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Password_protection">Password protection</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Password protection"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1305433154" /><table class="box-More&#95;citations&#95;needed&#95;section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/60px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/120px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Microsoft_Word" title="Special:EditPage/Microsoft Word">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2024</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office_password_protection" title="Microsoft Office password protection">Microsoft Office password protection</a></div>
<p>Three password types can be set in Microsoft Word:
</p>
<ul><li>Password to open a document<sup id="cite&#95;ref-office.com-password-prot&#95;89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-office.com-password-prot-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Password to modify a document<sup id="cite&#95;ref-office.com-password-prot&#95;89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-office.com-password-prot-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Password restricting formatting and editing<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The second and third password types were developed by Microsoft for convenient shared use of documents rather than for their protection. There is no <a href="/wiki/Encryption" title="Encryption">encryption</a> of documents that are protected by such passwords and the Microsoft Office protection system saves a <a href="/wiki/Hash_sum" class="mw-redirect" title="Hash sum">hash sum</a> of a password in a document's header where it can be easily accessed and removed by the specialized software. <i>Password to open a document</i> offers much tougher protection that had been steadily enhanced in the subsequent editions of Microsoft Office.
</p><p><i>Word 95</i> and all the preceding editions had the weakest protection that utilized a conversion of a password to a 16-bit <a href="/wiki/Encryption_key" class="mw-redirect" title="Encryption key">key</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Key_size" title="Key size">Key length</a> in <i>Word 97</i> and <i>2000</i> was strengthened up to 40 bit. However, modern cracking software allows removing such a password very quickly – a persistent cracking process takes one week at most. Use of <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_tables" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainbow tables">rainbow tables</a> reduces password removal time to several seconds. Some <a href="/wiki/Password_recovery" class="mw-redirect" title="Password recovery">password recovery</a> software can not only remove a password but also find an actual password that was used by a user to encrypt the document using the <a href="/wiki/Brute-force_attack" title="Brute-force attack">brute-force attack</a> approach. Statistically, the possibility of recovering the password depends on the <a href="/wiki/Password_strength" title="Password strength">password strength</a>.
</p><p>Word's 2003/XP version default protection remained the same but an option that allowed advanced users to choose a <a href="/wiki/Cryptographic_Service_Provider" title="Cryptographic Service Provider">Cryptographic Service Provider</a> was added.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> If a strong CSP is chosen, guaranteed document decryption becomes unavailable and, therefore, a password can't be removed from the document. Nonetheless, a password can be fairly quickly picked with a brute-force attack, because its speed is still high regardless of the CSP selected. Moreover, since the CSPs are not active by default, their use is limited to advanced users only.
</p><p>Word 2007 offers significantly more secure document protection which utilizes the modern <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Encryption_Standard" title="Advanced Encryption Standard">Advanced Encryption Standard</a> (AES) that converts a password to a 128-bit key using a <a href="/wiki/SHA-1" title="SHA-1">SHA-1</a> hash function 50,000 times. It makes password removal impossible (as of today, no computer that can pick the key in a reasonable amount of time exists) and drastically slows the brute-force attack speed down to several hundreds of passwords per second.
</p><p>Word's 2010 protection algorithm was not changed apart from the increasing number of SHA-1 conversions up to 100,000 times and consequently, the brute-force attack speed decreased two times more.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Versions_and_platforms">Versions and platforms</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Versions and platforms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Word_for_Windows">Word for Windows</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Word for Windows"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MS_Word_2007.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/23/MS_Word_2007.png/250px-MS_Word_2007.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/23/MS_Word_2007.png 1.5x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="257" /></a><figcaption>Microsoft Word for Windows (2007)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Word for Windows is available stand-alone or as part of the Microsoft Office suite. Word contains rudimentary desktop publishing capabilities and is the most widely used word processing program on the market. Word files are commonly used as the format for sending text documents via e-mail because almost every user with a computer can read a Word document by using the Word application, a Word viewer or a word processor that imports the Word format (see <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Word_Viewer" title="Microsoft Word Viewer">Microsoft Word Viewer</a>).
</p><p>Word 6 for <a href="/wiki/Windows_NT" title="Windows NT">Windows NT</a> was the first 32-bit version of the product,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> released with Microsoft Office for Windows NT around the same time as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows_95" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft Windows 95">Windows 95</a>. It was a straightforward port of Word 6.0. Starting with Word 95, each release of Word was named after the year of its release, instead of its version number.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word 2007 introduced a redesigned user interface that emphasized the most common controls, dividing them into tabs, and adding specific options depending on the context, such as selecting an image or editing a table.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-office2007ui2&#95;94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-office2007ui2-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This user interface, called Ribbon, was included in Excel, PowerPoint and Access 2007, and would be later introduced to other Office applications with <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office_2010" title="Microsoft Office 2010">Office 2010</a> and Windows applications such as Paint and WordPad with <a href="/wiki/Windows_7" title="Windows 7">Windows 7</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The redesigned interface also includes a toolbar that appears when selecting text, with options for formatting included.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-office2007ui&#95;96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-office2007ui-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word 2007 also included the option to save documents as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Acrobat" title="Adobe Acrobat">Adobe Acrobat</a> or XPS files,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-office2007ui&#95;96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-office2007ui-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and upload Word documents like blog posts on services such as WordPress.
</p><p>Word 2010 allows the customization of the Ribbon,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcmag&#95;office2010&#95;97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcmag_office2010-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> adds a Backstage view for file management,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcmag&#95;backstage&#95;98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcmag_backstage-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> has improved document navigation, allows creation and embedding of screenshots,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcmag&#95;word2010&#95;99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcmag_word2010-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and integrates with online services such as Microsoft <a href="/wiki/OneDrive" title="OneDrive">OneDrive</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word 2019 added a dictation function.
</p><p>Word 2021 added co-authoring, a visual refresh on the start experience and tabs, automatic cloud saving, dark mode, line focus, an updated draw tab, and support for ODF 1.3.
</p><p>Microsoft Word 2024 (Fourth perpetual release of Office 16) for the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">MacOS</a> was released on October 1, 2024.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Word_for_Mac">Word for Mac</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Word for Mac"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office#Mac_versions" title="Microsoft Office">Microsoft Office § Mac versions</a></div><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Word_for_Mac_screenshot.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/19/Word_for_Mac_screenshot.png/250px-Word_for_Mac_screenshot.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="140" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/19/Word_for_Mac_screenshot.png 1.5x" data-file-width="423" data-file-height="237" /></a><figcaption>Word for Mac running on <a href="/wiki/MacOS_Ventura" title="MacOS Ventura">macOS Ventura</a> (13.2)</figcaption></figure><p>The Mac was introduced on January 24, 1984, and Microsoft introduced Word 1.0 for Mac a year later, on January 18, 1985. The DOS, Mac, and Windows versions are quite different from each other. Only the Mac version was <a href="/wiki/WYSIWYG" title="WYSIWYG">WYSIWYG</a> and used a graphical user interface, far ahead of the other platforms. Each platform restarted its version numbering at "1.0".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There was no version 2 on the Mac, but version 3 came out on January 31, 1987, as described above. Word 4.0 came out on November 6, 1990, and added automatic linking with Excel, the ability to flow text around graphics, and a WYSIWYG page view editing mode. Word 5.1 for Mac, released in 1992 ran on the original 68000 CPU and was the last to be specifically designed as a Macintosh application. The later Word 6 was a Windows port and poorly received. Word 5.1 continued to run well until the last <a href="/wiki/Classic_Mac_OS" title="Classic Mac OS">classic Mac OS</a>. Many people continue to run Word 5.1 to this day under an emulated Mac classic system for some of its excellent features, such as document generation and renumbering, or to access their old files.
</p><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Microsoft_Word_for_Mac_2011.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2c/Microsoft_Word_for_Mac_2011.png/250px-Microsoft_Word_for_Mac_2011.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="181" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2c/Microsoft_Word_for_Mac_2011.png 1.5x" data-file-width="371" data-file-height="268" /></a><figcaption>Microsoft Word 2011 running on OS X</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1997, Microsoft formed the <a href="/wiki/Macintosh_Business_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Macintosh Business Unit">Macintosh Business Unit</a> as an independent group within Microsoft focused on writing software for the classic Mac OS. Its first version of Word, Word 98, was released with Office 98 Macintosh Edition. Document compatibility reached parity with Word 97,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ugeek&#95;97&#95;39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ugeek_97-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and it included features from Word 97 for Windows, including spell and grammar checking with squiggles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-appleinsider&#95;history&#95;103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleinsider_history-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Users could choose the menus and keyboard shortcuts to be similar to either Word 97 for Windows or Word 5 for Mac.
</p><p>Word 2001, released in 2000, added a few new features, including the <a href="/wiki/Clipboard_manager" title="Clipboard manager">Office Clipboard</a>, which allowed users to copy and paste multiple items.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-atpm&#95;104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atpm-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was the last version to run on the classic Mac OS and, on <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">Mac OS X</a>, it could only run within the <a href="/wiki/Classic_Environment" class="mw-redirect" title="Classic Environment">Classic Environment</a>. Word X, released in 2001, was the first version to run natively on, and to require, Mac OS X,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-appleinsider&#95;history&#95;103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleinsider_history-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and introduced non-contiguous text selection.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-macworld&#95;wordx&#95;105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macworld_wordx-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word 2004 was released in May 2004. It included a new Notebook Layout view for taking notes either by typing or by voice.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-macworld&#95;2004&#95;106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macworld_2004-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other features, such as tracking changes, were made more similar with Office for Windows.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-macnn&#95;2004&#95;107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macnn_2004-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word 2008, released on January 15, 2008, included a Ribbon-like feature, called the Elements Gallery, that can be used to select page layouts and insert custom diagrams and images. It also included a new view focused on publishing layout, integrated bibliography management,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-appleinsider&#95;word2008&#95;1&#95;108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleinsider_word2008_1-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and native support for the new Office Open XML format. It was the first version to run natively on Intel-based Macs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-appleinsider&#95;2008&#95;109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleinsider_2008-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word 2011, released in October 2010, replaced the Elements Gallery in favor of a Ribbon user interface that is much more similar to Office for Windows,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-appleinsider&#95;ribbon&#95;110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleinsider_ribbon-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and includes a full-screen mode that allows users to focus on reading and writing documents, and support for <a href="/wiki/Office_Web_Apps" class="mw-redirect" title="Office Web Apps">Office Web Apps</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-appleinsider&#95;2011&#95;2&#95;111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleinsider_2011_2-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft Office 2016 for Mac (2015)
</p><p>Microsoft Office 2019 for Mac (2018)
</p><p>Word 2021 added real-time co-authoring, automatic cloud saving, dark mode, immersive reader enhancements, line focus, a visual refresh, the ability to save pictures in SVG format, and a new Sketched style outline.
</p><p>Word 2024, released on September 16, 2024, included Word session recovery, support for ODF 1.4, new theme and color palette and ability for easier collaboration. Even though collaboration features were also available in Microsoft Word 2021 as part of post release update, they were not available in Word LTSC 2021 or Word LTSC 2024.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Write_for_Atari_ST">Write for Atari ST</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Write for Atari ST"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Microsoft_Word#Write_for_Atari_ST" title="History of Microsoft Word">History of Microsoft Word §&#160;Write for Atari ST</a></div><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MS_Write_on_Atari_ST.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/77/MS_Write_on_Atari_ST.png/250px-MS_Write_on_Atari_ST.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="156" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/77/MS_Write_on_Atari_ST.png 1.5x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="250" /></a><figcaption>Microsoft Word on Atari ST was titled Microsoft Write.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Microsoft Write for the <a href="/wiki/Atari_ST" title="Atari ST">Atari ST</a> is the Atari version of Microsoft Word 1.05 released for the Apple Macintosh while sharing the same name as the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Write" title="Microsoft Write">Microsoft Write</a> program included in Windows during the 80s and early 90s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While the program was announced in 1986, various delays caused the program to arrive in 1988.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Microsoft Write for Atari ST and Microsoft Word for Windows would both make their debut at the 1988 <a href="/wiki/COMDEX" title="COMDEX">COMDEX</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, Georgia alongside their respective booths.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Like the Mac version, the Atari version features <a href="/wiki/WYSIWYG" title="WYSIWYG">WYSIWYG</a> form (via <a href="/wiki/Graphics_Device_Operating_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics Device Operating System">GDOS</a>) and used a graphical user interface (via <a href="/wiki/Graphics_Environment_Manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics Environment Manager">GEM</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft Write was one of the first Atari word processors that utilizes the GDOS (<a href="/wiki/Graphics_Device_Operating_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics Device Operating System">Graphics Device Operating System</a>) part of GEM (<a href="/wiki/Graphics_Environment_Manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics Environment Manager">Graphics Environment Manager</a>) allowing the word processor to display and print graphic fonts &amp; styles making it a multifont word processor for the Atari ST (a 2nd disk drive was required to run both Microsoft Write and GDOS).  Microsoft Write was packaged with GDOS 1.1 and the drivers for the Atari XMM804 dot matrix printer along with 3rd party printers like <a href="/wiki/Epson" title="Epson">Epson</a> FX-80 and <a href="/wiki/Star_Micronics" title="Star Micronics">Star Micronics</a> NB-15 on 4 diskettes (3½ inch format).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Accompanying the retail packaging was a 206-page slip-cased <a href="/wiki/User_guide" title="User guide">user's manual</a> that was divided into 3 sections: Learning Write, Using Write and Write Reference.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  In addition, Microsoft Write also featured a "Help Screen" tool to help a user explore the advanced features of the word processor that earned high praise for its form and presentation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Write_for_Macintosh">Write for Macintosh</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Write for Macintosh"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In October 1987, Microsoft released Microsoft Write for Macintosh. Write is a version of Microsoft Word with limited features that Microsoft hoped would replace aging <a href="/wiki/MacWrite" title="MacWrite">MacWrite</a> in the Macintosh word processor market. Write was priced well below Word, though at the time MacWrite was included with new Macintoshes. Write is best described as Word locked in "Short Menus" mode, and as such it used the same file format so that users could exchange files with absolutely no conversion necessary.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Write did not sell well and was discontinued before the <a href="/wiki/System_7" title="System 7">System 7</a> era. Microsoft Write was part of a short-lived trend for "lightweight" Macintosh word processors initiated by the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Macintosh_Portable" title="Macintosh Portable">Macintosh Portable</a> and early <a href="/wiki/PowerBook" title="PowerBook">PowerBook</a> systems. Others included <a href="/wiki/LetterPerfect" class="mw-redirect" title="LetterPerfect">LetterPerfect</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nisus_Writer" title="Nisus Writer">Nisus Compact</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Word_on_mobile_platforms">Word on mobile platforms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Word on mobile platforms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pocket_Word_on_HPC.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5a/Pocket_Word_on_HPC.png/250px-Pocket_Word_on_HPC.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="94" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5a/Pocket_Word_on_HPC.png/500px-Pocket_Word_on_HPC.png 1.5x" data-file-width="516" data-file-height="193" /></a><figcaption>Microsoft Pocket Word running on <a href="/wiki/Handheld_PC" title="Handheld PC">Handheld PC 2000</a></figcaption></figure><p>
The first mobile versions of Word were released with <a href="/wiki/Windows_CE" title="Windows CE">Windows CE</a> in 1996 on <a href="/wiki/Handheld_PC" title="Handheld PC">Handheld PCs</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and later also on <a href="/wiki/Pocket_PC" title="Pocket PC">Pocket PCs</a>.</p><figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Word_for_Android.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Word_for_Android.png/120px-Word_for_Android.png" decoding="async" width="103" height="230" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/93/Word_for_Android.png 1.5x" data-file-width="212" data-file-height="471" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_365" title="Microsoft 365">Microsoft 365</a> version of Microsoft Word running on <a href="/wiki/Android_13" title="Android 13">Android 13</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The modern Word Mobile<sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> supports basic formatting, such as bolding, changing font size, and changing colors (from red, yellow, or green). It can add comments, but can't edit documents with tracked changes. It can't open password-protected documents; change the typeface, text alignment, or style (normal, heading 1); insert responsive checkboxes; insert pictures; or undo.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-TechHive&#95;125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TechHive-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Engadget&#95;126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engadget-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-NYT&#95;127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word Mobile is neither able to display nor insert <a href="/wiki/Footnote" class="mw-redirect" title="Footnote">footnotes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endnote" class="mw-redirect" title="Endnote">endnotes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Page_footer" title="Page footer">page footers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Page_break" title="Page break">page breaks</a>, certain <a href="/wiki/Indentation_(typesetting)" title="Indentation (typesetting)">indentation</a> of lists, and certain <a href="/wiki/Font" title="Font">fonts</a> while working on a document, but retains them if the original document has them.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Unsupported&#95;Word&#95;Mobile&#95;features&#95;129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unsupported_Word_Mobile_features-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Word Mobile can insert lists, but doesn't allow to set custom bullet symbols and customize list numbering. In addition to the features of the 2013 version, the 2007 version on Windows Mobile also has the ability to save documents in the <a href="/wiki/Rich_Text_Format" title="Rich Text Format">Rich Text Format</a> and open legacy PSW (Pocket Word).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Unsupported&#95;Word&#95;Mobile&#95;features&#95;129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unsupported_Word_Mobile_features-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Furthermore, it includes a <a href="/wiki/Spell_checker" title="Spell checker">spell checker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Word_count" title="Word count">word count</a> tool, and a "Find and Replace" command. In 2015, Word Mobile became available for Windows 10 and Windows 10 Mobile on <a href="/wiki/Windows_Store" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows Store">Windows Store</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Support for the <a href="/wiki/Windows_10_Mobile" title="Windows 10 Mobile">Windows 10 Mobile</a> version ended on January 12, 2021.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Word for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> was released on March 27, 2014<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and for <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> was released on January 29, 2015.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Word_for_the_web">Word for the web</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Word for the web"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office#Office_on_the_web" title="Microsoft Office">Microsoft Office §&#160;Office on the web</a></div>
<p>Word for the web is a free lightweight version of Microsoft Word available as part of Office on the web, which also includes web versions of Microsoft Excel and Microsoft PowerPoint.
</p><p>Word for the web lacks some Ribbon tabs, such as Design and Mailings. Mailings allows users to print envelopes and labels and manage mail merge <a href="/wiki/Printing" title="Printing">printing</a> of Word documents.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcworld.com&#95;134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcworld.com-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-pcworld.com3&#95;135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcworld.com3-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Word for the web is not able to edit certain objects, such as: equations, shapes, text boxes or drawings, but a placeholder may be present in the document. Certain advanced features like table sorting or columns will not be displayed but are preserved as they were in the document. Other views available in the Word desktop app (Outline, Draft, Web Layout, and Full-Screen Reading) are not available, nor are side-by-side viewing, split windows, and the ruler.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-osupport-word&#95;136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osupport-word-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reception">Reception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Reception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Initial releases of Word were met with criticism. <a href="/wiki/Byte_(magazine)" title="Byte (magazine)">Byte</a> in 1984 criticized the documentation for Word 1.1 and 2.0 for DOS, calling it "a complete farce". It called the software "clever, put together well and performs some extraordinary feats", but concluded that "especially when operated with the mouse, has many more limitations than benefits... extremely frustrating to learn and operate efficiently".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cameron1984pc&#95;137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cameron1984pc-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/PC_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="PC Magazine">PC Magazine</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> review was very mixed, stating: "I've run into weird word processors before, but this is the first time one's nearly knocked me down for the count" but acknowledging that Word's innovations were the first that caused the reviewer to consider abandoning <a href="/wiki/WordStar" title="WordStar">WordStar</a>. While the review cited an excellent <a href="/wiki/WYSIWYG" title="WYSIWYG">WYSIWYG</a> display, sophisticated print formatting, windows, and footnoting as merits, it criticized many small flaws, very slow performance, and "documentation produced by Madame Sadie's Pain Palace". It concluded that Word was "two releases away from potential greatness".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-manes19840221&#95;138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manes19840221-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jerry_Pournelle" title="Jerry Pournelle">Jerry Pournelle</a> wrote in October 1987 said that he did not like Word because "the mouse is such an integral part of the program. When I am creating text, I do <i>not</i> want to take my hands off the keyboard".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pournelle198710&#95;139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pournelle198710-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Compute!'s Apple Applications</i> in December 1987 stated that "despite a certain awkwardness", Word 3.01 "will likely become the major Macintosh word processor" with "far too many features to list here". While criticizing the lack of true WYSIWYG, the magazine concluded that "<i>Word</i> is marvelous. It's like a <a href="/wiki/Mozart" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozart">Mozart</a> or <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Edison</a>, whose occasional gaucherie we excuse because of his great gifts".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-mcneill198712&#95;140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcneill198712-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Compute!" title="Compute!">Compute!</a></i> in 1989 stated that Word 5.0's integration of text and graphics made it "a solid engine for basic desktop publishing". The magazine approved of improvements to text mode, described the $75 price for upgrading from an earlier version as "the deal of the decade" and concluded that "as a high-octane word processor, <i>Word</i> is worth a look".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nimersheim198912&#95;141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nimersheim198912-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Computer Intelligence estimated in 1987 that Microsoft had 4% of the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_1000" title="Fortune 1000">Fortune 1000</a> PC word processor market.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-computerworld19871102interview&#95;142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld19871102interview-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 1988 <i>PC</i> reader survey found that 11% used Word, third behind WordPerfect and WordStar.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-seymour19880229&#95;28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seymour19880229-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 1990 <a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Certified_Public_Accountants" title="American Institute of Certified Public Accountants">American Institute of Certified Public Accountants</a> member survey found that 8% used Word, in third place behind WordPerfect and WordStar.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-aicpa1990&#95;143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aicpa1990-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dataquest" title="Dataquest">Dataquest</a> estimated that Word had 55% of the Windows word processor market in 1991.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-cw19920720&#95;36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cw19920720-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the first quarter of 1996, Word accounted for 80% of the worldwide word processor market.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Microsoft added Word to the new <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_365" title="Microsoft 365">Office 365</a> product, where Microsoft has combined their most popular software,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which is a <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud based</a> computing software that is subscription-based to compete with <a href="/wiki/Google_Docs" title="Google Docs">Google Docs</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Release_history">Release history</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Word&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Release history"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
